<p>This focus on the infantry is matched with the doctrine of "Every Marine [is] a rifleman", a focus of Commandant <a href="/wiki/Alfred_M._Gray,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Alfred M. Gray, Jr.">Alfred M. Gray, Jr.</a>, emphasizing the infantry combat abilities of every Marine. All Marines, regardless of military specialization, receive training as a <a href="/wiki/Rifleman" title="Rifleman">rifleman</a>; and all officers receive additional training as infantry platoon commanders.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> For example, at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Wake_Island" title="Battle of Wake Island">Wake Island</a>, when all of the Marine aircraft were destroyed, pilots continued the fight as ground officers, leading supply clerks and cooks in a final defensive effort.<sup id="cite_ref-Heinl_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heinl-31">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> Flexibility of execution is implemented via an emphasis on "<a href="/wiki/Commander%27s_intent" class="mw-redirect" title="Commander&#39;s intent">commander's intent</a>" as a guiding principle for carrying out orders; specifying the end state but leaving open the method of execution.<sup id="cite_ref-Lind_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lind-32">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The amphibious assault techniques developed for World War II evolved, with the addition of <a href="/wiki/Air_assault" title="Air assault">air assault</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maneuver_warfare" title="Maneuver warfare">maneuver warfare</a> doctrine, into the current "<i>Operational Maneuver from the Sea</i>" doctrine of <a href="/wiki/Power_projection" title="Power projection">power projection</a> from the seas.<sup id="cite_ref-OMFTS_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OMFTS-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The Marines are credited with the development of helicopter insertion doctrine and were the earliest in the American military to widely adopt maneuver-warfare principles, which emphasize low-level initiative and flexible execution. In light of recent warfare that has strayed from the Corps's traditional missions,<sup id="cite_ref-2ndarmy_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2ndarmy-33">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> it has renewed an emphasis on amphibious capabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USMC-041227-M-0484L-006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/USMC-041227-M-0484L-006.jpg/220px-USMC-041227-M-0484L-006.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/USMC-041227-M-0484L-006.jpg/330px-USMC-041227-M-0484L-006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d4/USMC-041227-M-0484L-006.jpg/440px-USMC-041227-M-0484L-006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1312" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USMC-041227-M-0484L-006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Machine gunner from 1st Platoon, Company B, 1st Battalion, 23rd Marine Regiment in cold weather gear armed with a Squad Automatic Weapon taking part in a security patrol around Ramadi, Iraq, 27 December 2006</div></div></div>
<p>The Marine Corps relies on the Navy for <a href="/wiki/Sealift" title="Sealift">sealift</a> to provide its rapid deployment capabilities. In addition to basing a third of the <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Marine_Force" title="Fleet Marine Force">Fleet Marine Force</a> in Japan, <a href="/wiki/Marine_Expeditionary_Unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine Expeditionary Unit">Marine Expeditionary Units</a> (MEU) are typically stationed at sea so they can function as first responders to international incidents.<sup id="cite_ref-ChenowethNihart_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChenowethNihart-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> To aid rapid deployment, the <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Pre-Positioning_System" class="mw-redirect" title="Maritime Pre-Positioning System">Maritime Pre-Positioning System</a> was developed: fleets of <a href="/wiki/Container_ship" title="Container ship">container ships</a> are positioned throughout the world with enough equipment and supplies for a <a href="/wiki/Marine_Expeditionary_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine Expeditionary Force">Marine Expeditionary Force</a> to deploy for 30 days.
</p><p>The USMC is planning to reduce its logistical requirements and by 2025 eliminate all liquid fuel use for Marine Expeditionary Forces, except for highly efficient vehicles.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Doctrine">Doctrine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Doctrine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Two small manuals published during the 1930s would establish USMC doctrine in two areas. The <i><a href="/wiki/Small_Wars_Manual" title="Small Wars Manual">Small Wars Manual</a></i> laid the framework for Marine <a href="/wiki/Counter-insurgency" title="Counter-insurgency">counter-insurgency</a> operations from Vietnam to Iraq and Afghanistan while the <a href="/wiki/Amphibious_warfare_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Amphibious warfare (United States)">Tentative Landing Operations Manual</a> established the doctrine for the amphibious operations of World War II. "<i>Operational Maneuver from the Sea</i>" is the current doctrine of power projection.<sup id="cite_ref-OMFTS_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OMFTS-13">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_United_States_Marine_Corps" title="History of the United States Marine Corps">History of the United States Marine Corps</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">Origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Nassau.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Painting of Continental Marines landing on a tropical beach from rowboats, with two ships in the background" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Battle_of_Nassau.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Nassau.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Battle_of_Nassau.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Nassau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Battle_of_Nassau.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Nassau.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4971" data-file-height="3285" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Nassau.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Continental_Marines" title="Continental Marines">Continental Marines</a> land at <a href="/wiki/New_Providence" title="New Providence">New Providence</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Nassau" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Nassau">Battle of Nassau</a>, the first amphibious landing of the Marine Corps, during the revolution</div></div></div>
<p>The United States Marine Corps traces its roots to the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Marines" title="Continental Marines">Continental Marines</a> of the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, formed by Captain <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Nicholas" title="Samuel Nicholas">Samuel Nicholas</a> by a resolution of the <a href="/wiki/Second_Continental_Congress" title="Second Continental Congress">Second Continental Congress</a> on 10 November 1775, to raise two <a href="/wiki/Battalion" title="Battalion">battalions</a> of Marines. That date is regarded and celebrated as the date of the Marine Corps's <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps_birthday_ball" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Marine Corps birthday ball">birthday</a>. At the end of the American Revolution, both the <a href="/wiki/Continental_Navy" title="Continental Navy">Continental Navy</a> and Continental Marines were disbanded in April 1783. The institution itself would not be resurrected until 11 July 1798. At that time, in preparation for the <a href="/wiki/Quasi-War" title="Quasi-War">Quasi-War</a> with <a href="/wiki/First_French_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="First French Republic">France</a>, Congress created the United States Marine Corps.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> Marines had been enlisted by the War Department as early as August 1797<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> for service in the new-build <a href="/wiki/Frigate" title="Frigate">frigates</a> authorized by the Congressional "Act to provide a Naval Armament" of 18 March 1794,<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> which specified the numbers of Marines to recruit for each frigate.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Attack_on_Derna_by_Charles_Waterhouse_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Attack_on_Derna_by_Charles_Waterhouse_01.jpg/220px-Attack_on_Derna_by_Charles_Waterhouse_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Attack_on_Derna_by_Charles_Waterhouse_01.jpg/330px-Attack_on_Derna_by_Charles_Waterhouse_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Attack_on_Derna_by_Charles_Waterhouse_01.jpg/440px-Attack_on_Derna_by_Charles_Waterhouse_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="720" data-file-height="482" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Attack_on_Derna_by_Charles_Waterhouse_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marines leading Arab mercenaries to victory under U.S. Navy Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/William_Eaton_(soldier)" title="William Eaton (soldier)">William Eaton</a> and U.S. Marine Corps First Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Presley_O%27Bannon" title="Presley O&#39;Bannon">Presley O'Bannon</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Derna_(1805)" title="Battle of Derna (1805)">Battle of Derna</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_Capture_Penguin.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Wiki_Capture_Penguin.jpg/220px-Wiki_Capture_Penguin.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Wiki_Capture_Penguin.jpg/330px-Wiki_Capture_Penguin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Wiki_Capture_Penguin.jpg/440px-Wiki_Capture_Penguin.jpg 2x" data-file-width="740" data-file-height="585" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_Capture_Penguin.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British and U.S. troops garrisoned aboard <i>Hornet</i> and <i>Penguin</i> exchanging <a href="/wiki/Small_arms" class="mw-redirect" title="Small arms">small arms</a> musket fire with Tristan da Cuna in the background during the <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_HMS_Penguin" title="Capture of HMS Penguin">final engagement</a> between British and U.S. forces in the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Marines' most famous action of this period occurred during the <a href="/wiki/First_Barbary_War" title="First Barbary War">First Barbary War</a> (1801–1805) against the <a href="/wiki/Barbary_pirate" class="mw-redirect" title="Barbary pirate">Barbary pirates</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> when <a href="/wiki/William_Eaton_(soldier)" title="William Eaton (soldier)">William Eaton</a> and First Lieutenant <a href="/wiki/Presley_O%27Bannon" title="Presley O&#39;Bannon">Presley O'Bannon</a> led eight Marines and 500 <a href="/wiki/Mercenary" title="Mercenary">mercenaries</a> in an effort to capture <a href="/wiki/Tripoli" title="Tripoli">Tripoli</a>. Though they only reached <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Derne" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Derne">Derna</a>, the action at Tripoli has been immortalized in the <a href="/wiki/Marines%27_hymn" class="mw-redirect" title="Marines&#39; hymn">Marines' hymn</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mameluke_sword" title="Mameluke sword">Mameluke sword</a> carried by Marine officers.<sup id="cite_ref-Simmons_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Simmons-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>, Marine detachments on Navy ships took part in some of the great frigate duels that characterized the war, which were the first and last engagements of the conflict. Their most significant contribution, however, was holding the center of General <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Jackson" title="Andrew Jackson">Jackson</a>'s defensive line at the 1815 <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_New_Orleans" title="Battle of New Orleans">Battle of New Orleans</a>, the final major battle and one of the most one-sided engagements of the war. With widespread news of the battle and the <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_HMS_Cyane_and_HMS_Levant" title="Capture of HMS Cyane and HMS Levant">capture of HMS <i>Cyane</i>, HMS <i>Levant</i></a> and <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_HMS_Penguin" title="Capture of HMS Penguin">HMS <i>Penguin</i></a>, the final engagements between British and U.S. forces, the Marines had gained a reputation as expert <a href="/wiki/Marksman" title="Marksman">marksmen</a>, especially in defensive and ship-to-ship actions.<sup id="cite_ref-Simmons_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Simmons-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> They played a large role in the 1813 <a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Sacket%27s_Harbor" title="Second Battle of Sacket&#39;s Harbor">defense of Sacket's Harbor</a>, New York and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Craney_Island" title="Battle of Craney Island">Norfolk and Portsmouth</a>, Virginia,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> also taking part in the 1814 <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Plattsburgh" title="Battle of Plattsburgh">defense of Plattsburgh</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Champlain_Valley" title="Champlain Valley">Champlain Valley</a> during one of the final British offensives along the Canadian-American border.
</p><p>After the war, the Marine Corps fell into a malaise that ended with the appointment of <a href="/wiki/Archibald_Henderson" title="Archibald Henderson">Archibald Henderson</a> as its fifth Commandant in 1820. Under his tenure, the Corps took on expeditionary duties in the Caribbean, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">Gulf of Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Key_West,_Florida" class="mw-redirect" title="Key West, Florida">Key West</a>, West Africa, the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sumatra" title="Sumatra">Sumatra</a>. Commandant Henderson is credited with thwarting President Jackson's attempts to combine and integrate the Marine Corps with the Army.<sup id="cite_ref-Simmons_41-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Simmons-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Instead, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">Congress</a> passed the <i>Act for the Better Organization of the Marine Corps</i> in 1834, stipulating that the Corps was part of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Navy" title="United States Department of the Navy">Department of the Navy</a> as a sister service to the Navy.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> This would be the first of many times that the independent existence of the Corps was challenged.
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chapultepec.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Chapultepec.jpg/220px-Chapultepec.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Chapultepec.jpg/330px-Chapultepec.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Chapultepec.jpg/440px-Chapultepec.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3019" data-file-height="1971" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chapultepec.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. Marines <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chapultepec" title="Battle of Chapultepec">storming Chapultepec castle</a> under a large American flag, paving the way for the fall of Mexico City</div></div></div>
<p>Commandant Henderson volunteered the Marines for service in the <a href="/wiki/Seminole_Wars" title="Seminole Wars">Seminole Wars</a> of 1835, personally leading nearly half of the entire Corps (two battalions) to war. A decade later, in the <a href="/wiki/Mexican%E2%80%93American_War" title="Mexican–American War">Mexican–American War</a> (1846–1848), the Marines made their famed <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chapultepec" title="Battle of Chapultepec">assault on Chapultepec Palace</a> in Mexico City, which would be later celebrated as the "Halls of Montezuma" in the Marines' hymn. In the 1850s, the Marines would see further service in Panama and Asia, attached to <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Calbraith_Perry" class="mw-redirect" title="Matthew Calbraith Perry">Matthew Perry's</a> <a href="/wiki/East_India_Squadron" title="East India Squadron">East India Squadron</a> on its historic trip to the Far East.<sup id="cite_ref-Moskin_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moskin-44">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="American_Civil_War_to_World_War_I">American Civil War to World War I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: American Civil War to World War I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marines01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="black &amp; white photograph of six U.S. marines standing in line, five with Civil War-era rifles and one with an NCO sword." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Marines01.jpg/220px-Marines01.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Marines01.jpg/330px-Marines01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Marines01.jpg/440px-Marines01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5900" data-file-height="4550" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marines01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Five USMC privates with fixed <a href="/wiki/Bayonet" title="Bayonet">bayonets</a>, and their NCO with his sword at the <a href="/wiki/Washington_Navy_Yard" title="Washington Navy Yard">Washington Navy Yard</a>, 1864</div></div></div>
<p>The Marine Corps played a small role in the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">Civil War</a> (1861–1865); their most prominent task was <a href="/wiki/Blockade" title="Blockade">blockade</a> duty. As more and more states <a href="/wiki/Ordinance_of_Secession" title="Ordinance of Secession">seceded</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">Union</a>, about a third of the Corps's officers left the United States to join the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederacy</a> and form the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_Marine_Corps" title="Confederate States Marine Corps">Confederate States Marine Corps</a>, which ultimately played little part in the war. The battalion of recruits formed for the <a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_Bull_Run" title="First Battle of Bull Run">First Battle of Bull Run</a> (also known as the First Battle of Manassas<sup id="cite_ref-1stmanassas_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1stmanassas-45">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> by the Confederate forces), performed poorly, retreating with the rest of the Union forces.<sup id="cite_ref-ChenowethNihart_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChenowethNihart-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Blockade duty included sea-based amphibious operations to secure forward bases. In late November 1861, Marines and sailors landed a reconnaissance in force from the <a href="/wiki/USS_Flag_(1861)" title="USS Flag (1861)">USS&#160;<i>Flag</i></a> at Tybee Island, Georgia, to occupy the Lighthouse and Martello Tower on the northern end of the island. It would later be the Army base for bombardment of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Pulaski" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Fort Pulaski">Fort Pulaski</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In April and May 1862, Union Marines participated in the <a href="/wiki/Capture_of_New_Orleans" title="Capture of New Orleans">capture and occupation of New Orleans</a> and the occupation of Baton Rouge, Louisiana<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> signal events in the war that helped secure Union control of the lower Mississippi River basin and denied the Confederacy a major port and naval base on the Gulf coast.
</p><p>The remainder of the 19th century was marked by declining strength and introspection about the mission of the Marine Corps. The Navy's transition from <a href="/wiki/Sailing_ship" title="Sailing ship">sail</a> to <a href="/wiki/Steamboat" title="Steamboat">steam</a> put into question the need for Marines on naval ships. Meanwhile, Marines served as a convenient resource for interventions and landings to protect American interests overseas. The Corps was involved in over 28 separate interventions in the 30 years from the end of the American Civil War to the end of 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> They would be called upon to stem political and labor unrest within the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Ellsworth_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ellsworth-49">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Under Commandant <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Zeilin" title="Jacob Zeilin">Jacob Zeilin</a>'s tenure, Marine customs and traditions took shape: the Corps adopted the <a href="/wiki/Eagle,_Globe,_and_Anchor" title="Eagle, Globe, and Anchor">Marine Corps emblem</a> on 19 November 1868. It was during this time that "<a href="/wiki/Marines%27_hymn" class="mw-redirect" title="Marines&#39; hymn">The Marines' Hymn</a>" was first heard. Around 1883, the Marines adopted their current motto "<i><a href="/wiki/Semper_Fidelis" class="mw-redirect" title="Semper Fidelis">Semper Fidelis</a></i>" (<i>Always Faithful</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-Simmons_41-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Simmons-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/John_Philip_Sousa" title="John Philip Sousa">John Philip Sousa</a>, the musician and composer, enlisted as a Marine apprentice at the age of 13, serving from 1867 until 1872, and again from 1880 to 1892 as the leader of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Band" title="United States Marine Band">Marine Band</a>. During the <a href="/wiki/Spanish%E2%80%93American_War" title="Spanish–American War">Spanish–American War</a> (1898), Marines led American forces ashore in the Philippines, Cuba, and <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">Puerto Rico</a>, demonstrating their readiness for deployment. At <a href="/wiki/Guant%C3%A1namo_Bay" title="Guantánamo Bay">Guantánamo Bay</a>, Cuba, the Marines seized an <a href="/wiki/Guantanamo_Bay_Naval_Base" title="Guantanamo Bay Naval Base">advanced naval base</a> that remains in use today. Between 1899 and 1916, the Corps continued its record of participation in foreign expeditions, including the <a href="/wiki/Philippine%E2%80%93American_War" title="Philippine–American War">Philippine–American War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Boxer_Rebellion" title="Boxer Rebellion">Boxer Rebellion</a> in China (1899–1901), Panama, the Cuban Pacifications, the <a href="/wiki/Perdicaris_incident" class="mw-redirect" title="Perdicaris incident">Perdicaris incident</a> in Morocco, <a href="/wiki/United_States_occupation_of_Veracruz" title="United States occupation of Veracruz">Veracruz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Santo_Domingo" title="Santo Domingo">Santo Domingo</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Banana_Wars" title="Banana Wars">Banana Wars</a> in <a href="/wiki/United_States_occupation_of_Haiti" title="United States occupation of Haiti">Haiti</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_occupation_of_Nicaragua" title="United States occupation of Nicaragua">Nicaragua</a>; the experiences gained in <a href="/wiki/Counter-insurgency" title="Counter-insurgency">counter-insurgency</a> and guerrilla operations during this period were consolidated into the <i><a href="/wiki/Small_Wars_Manual" title="Small Wars Manual">Small Wars Manual</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_I">World War I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: World War I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scott_Belleau_Wood.jpg" class="image"><img alt="monochromatic artwork of Marines fighting Germans in a forest" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Scott_Belleau_Wood.jpg/220px-Scott_Belleau_Wood.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Scott_Belleau_Wood.jpg/330px-Scott_Belleau_Wood.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Scott_Belleau_Wood.jpg/440px-Scott_Belleau_Wood.jpg 2x" data-file-width="896" data-file-height="674" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scott_Belleau_Wood.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Georges Scott, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Belleau_Wood" title="Battle of Belleau Wood"><i>American Marines in Belleau Wood</i></a>, 1918</div></div></div>
<p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> Marines served as a part of the <a href="/wiki/American_Expeditionary_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="American Expeditionary Force">American Expeditionary Force</a> under <a href="/wiki/General_Pershing" class="mw-redirect" title="General Pershing">General Pershing</a> when <a href="/wiki/American_entry_into_World_War_I" title="American entry into World War I">America entered into the war</a> on 6 April 1917. The Marine Corps had a deep pool of officers and NCOs with battle experience, and experienced a large expansion. During the war, the Marines, fighting on the <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Western Front (World War I)">Western Front</a> in France, fought at the battle at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Belleau_Wood" title="Battle of Belleau Wood">Belleau Wood</a> in mid-1918. Though the Marines and U.S. media reported that Germans had nicknamed them <i>Teufel Hunden</i> as meaning "<a href="/wiki/Devil_Dog" title="Devil Dog">Devil Dogs</a>", for their reputation as shock troops and marksmen at ranges up to 900 meters, there is no evidence of this in German records (as <i>Teufelshunde</i> would be the proper German phrase). Nevertheless, the name stuck in U.S. Marine lore.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_States_Marine_Corps_(1914-1939).png" class="image"><img alt="float" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Flag_of_the_United_States_Marine_Corps_%281914-1939%29.png/180px-Flag_of_the_United_States_Marine_Corps_%281914-1939%29.png" decoding="async" width="180" height="107" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/dd/Flag_of_the_United_States_Marine_Corps_%281914-1939%29.png 1.5x" data-file-width="267" data-file-height="159" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_States_Marine_Corps_(1914-1939).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/FIAV_historical.svg/23px-FIAV_historical.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Design used in the past, but now abandoned" width="23" height="15" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/FIAV_historical.svg/36px-FIAV_historical.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/FIAV_historical.svg/46px-FIAV_historical.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="230" data-file-height="150" /> The flag of the United States Marine Corps from 1914 to 1939</div></div></div>
<p>The U.S. Marine Corps entered the war with 511 officers and 13,214 enlisted personnel, and by 11 November 1918 had reached a strength of 2,400 officers and 70,000 enlisted.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> African-Americans were entirely excluded from the Marine Corps during this conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Opha_May_Johnson" title="Opha May Johnson">Opha May Johnson</a> was the first woman to enlist in the Marines; she joined the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Forces_Reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine Forces Reserve">Marine Corps Reserve</a> in 1918 during World War I, officially becoming the first female Marine.<sup id="cite_ref-History_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History-54">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> From then until the end of World War I, 305 women enlisted in the Corps.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">Between the World Wars</a>, the Marine Corps was headed by Commandant <a href="/wiki/John_A._Lejeune" title="John A. Lejeune">John A. Lejeune</a>, and under his leadership, the Corps studied and developed amphibious techniques that would be of great use in World War II. Many officers, including Lieutenant Colonel <a href="/wiki/Earl_Hancock_Ellis" title="Earl Hancock Ellis">Earl Hancock "Pete" Ellis</a>, foresaw a war in the Pacific with <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japan</a> and undertook preparations for such a conflict. Through 1941, as the prospect of war grew, the Corps pushed urgently for joint amphibious exercises with the Army and acquired amphibious equipment that would prove of great use in the upcoming conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-Ballendorf_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ballendorf-56">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II">World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Peter_Ortiz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Peter_Ortiz.jpg/150px-Peter_Ortiz.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="241" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0c/Peter_Ortiz.jpg/225px-Peter_Ortiz.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/0c/Peter_Ortiz.jpg 2x" data-file-width="299" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Peter_Ortiz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Former <a href="/wiki/List_of_French_Paratrooper_Units" class="mw-redirect" title="List of French Paratrooper Units">French Foreign Legion</a> Lieutenant, and U.S. Marine Corps officer <a href="/wiki/Peter_J._Ortiz" title="Peter J. Ortiz">Peter J. Ortiz</a>, who served in the European theater, often behind enemy lines</div></div></div>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, the Marines performed a central role in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_War" title="Pacific War">Pacific War</a>, along with the U.S. Army. The battles of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guadalcanal" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Guadalcanal">Guadalcanal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bougainville_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Bougainville Campaign">Bougainville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tarawa" title="Battle of Tarawa">Tarawa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Guam_(1944)" title="Battle of Guam (1944)">Guam</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Tinian" title="Battle of Tinian">Tinian</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Britain_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="New Britain Campaign">Cape Gloucester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Saipan" title="Battle of Saipan">Saipan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Peleliu" title="Battle of Peleliu">Peleliu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Iwo_Jima" title="Battle of Iwo Jima">Iwo Jima</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Okinawa" title="Battle of Okinawa">Okinawa</a> saw fierce fighting between Marines and the <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army" title="Imperial Japanese Army">Imperial Japanese Army</a>. Some 600,000 Americans served in the U.S. Marine Corps in World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Battle of Iwo Jima, which began on 19 February 1945, was arguably the most famous Marine engagement of the war.  The Japanese had learned from their defeats in the <a href="/wiki/Marianas_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Marianas Campaign">Marianas Campaign</a> and prepared many fortified positions on the island including <a href="/wiki/Pillbox_(military)" title="Pillbox (military)">pillboxes</a> and network of underground tunnels. The Japanese put up fierce resistance, but American forces reached the summit of Mount Suribachi on 23 February. The mission was accomplished with high losses of 26,000 American casualties and 22,000 Japanese.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Marines played a comparatively minor role in the <a href="/wiki/European_theatre_of_World_War_II" title="European theatre of World War II">European theater</a>. Nonetheless, they did continue to provide security detachments to U.S. embassies, and ships, contributed personnel to small, <a href="/wiki/Special_ops" class="mw-redirect" title="Special ops">special ops</a> teams dropped into <a href="/wiki/Nazi" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi">Nazi</a>-occupied Europe as part of <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Strategic_Services" title="Office of Strategic Services">Office of Strategic Services</a> (OSS, precursor to the <a href="/wiki/CIA" class="mw-redirect" title="CIA">CIA</a>) missions, and acted as staff planners, and trainers for U.S. Army amphibious operations, including the <a href="/wiki/Normandy_landings" title="Normandy landings">Normandy landings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>By the end of the war, the Corps expanded from two brigades to six <a href="/wiki/Division_(military)" title="Division (military)">divisions</a>, five <a href="/wiki/Wing_(air_force_unit)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wing (air force unit)">air wings</a>, and supporting troops, totaling about 485,000 Marines. In addition, 20 <a href="/wiki/Marine_defense_battalions" title="Marine defense battalions">defense battalions</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Paramarines" title="Paramarines">parachute battalion</a> were raised.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> Nearly 87,000 Marines were casualties during World War II (including nearly 20,000 killed), and 82 were awarded the <a href="/wiki/Medal_of_Honor" title="Medal of Honor">Medal of Honor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USMC_War_Memorial_Night.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Color photo of the Marine Corps War Memorial, a bronze statue of six Marines raising a U.S. flag attached unto a Japanese pipe atop Mount Suribachi." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/USMC_War_Memorial_Night.jpg/220px-USMC_War_Memorial_Night.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/USMC_War_Memorial_Night.jpg/330px-USMC_War_Memorial_Night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/USMC_War_Memorial_Night.jpg/440px-USMC_War_Memorial_Night.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USMC_War_Memorial_Night.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Photograph of the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_War_Memorial" title="Marine Corps War Memorial">Marine Corps War Memorial</a>, which depicts the second U.S. flag-raising atop <a href="/wiki/Mount_Suribachi" title="Mount Suribachi">Mount Suribachi</a>, on Iwo Jima. The memorial is modeled on <a href="/wiki/Joe_Rosenthal" title="Joe Rosenthal">Joe Rosenthal</a>'s famous <a href="/wiki/Raising_the_Flag_on_Iwo_Jima" title="Raising the Flag on Iwo Jima">Raising the Flag on Iwo Jima</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>In 1942, the Navy <a href="/wiki/Seabees" class="mw-redirect" title="Seabees">Seabees</a> were created with the Marine Corps providing their organization and military training.  Many Seabee units were issued the USMC standard issue and were re-designated "Marine". Despite the Corps's giving them their military organization, military training, issuing them uniforms and redesignating their units the Seabees remained Navy.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;note 3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-history.navy.mil_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-history.navy.mil-65">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> USMC historian Gordon L. Rottmann wrote that one of the "Navy's biggest contributions to the Marine Corps during WWII was the creation of the Seabees."<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Despite <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_the_Navy" class="mw-redirect" title="Secretary of the Navy">Secretary of the Navy</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Forrestal" title="James Forrestal">James Forrestal</a>'s prediction that the Marine flag raising at Iwo Jima meant "a Marine Corps for the next five hundred years",<sup id="cite_ref-Warren2007_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Warren2007-67">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Clancy1996_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Clancy1996-68">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> the Corps faced an immediate institutional crisis following the war due to a suddenly shrunken budget. Army generals pushing for a strengthened and reorganized defense establishment attempted to fold the Marine mission and assets into the Navy and Army. Drawing on hastily assembled Congressional support, and with the assistance of the so-called "<a href="/wiki/Revolt_of_the_Admirals" title="Revolt of the Admirals">Revolt of the Admirals</a>", the Marine Corps rebuffed such efforts to dismantle the Corps, resulting in statutory protection of the Marine Corps in the <a href="/wiki/National_Security_Act_of_1947" title="National Security Act of 1947">National Security Act of 1947</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Krulak_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krulak-69">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Shortly afterward, in 1952 the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Douglas%E2%80%93Mansfield_Act&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Douglas–Mansfield Act (page does not exist)">Douglas–Mansfield Act</a> afforded the Commandant an equal voice with the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff" title="Joint Chiefs of Staff">Joint Chiefs of Staff</a> on matters relating to the Marines and established the structure of <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Marine_Corps_divisions" title="List of United States Marine Corps divisions">three active divisions</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Marine_Corps_aircraft_wings" title="List of United States Marine Corps aircraft wings">air wings</a> that remain today.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Korean_War">Korean War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Korean War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Koreacloseairsupport1950.JPEG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Koreacloseairsupport1950.JPEG/220px-Koreacloseairsupport1950.JPEG" decoding="async" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Koreacloseairsupport1950.JPEG/330px-Koreacloseairsupport1950.JPEG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Koreacloseairsupport1950.JPEG/440px-Koreacloseairsupport1950.JPEG 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2332" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Koreacloseairsupport1950.JPEG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Vought_F4U_Corsair" title="Vought F4U Corsair">F4U Corsairs</a> provide close air support to Marines of the <a href="/wiki/1st_Marine_Division" title="1st Marine Division">1st Marine Division</a> fighting Chinese forces in North Korea, December 1950</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">Korean War</a> (1950–1953) saw the hastily formed <a href="/wiki/1st_Provisional_Marine_Brigade" title="1st Provisional Marine Brigade">Provisional Marine Brigade</a> holding the defensive line at the <a href="/wiki/Pusan_Perimeter" class="mw-redirect" title="Pusan Perimeter">Pusan Perimeter</a>. To execute a <a href="/wiki/Flanking_maneuver" title="Flanking maneuver">flanking maneuver</a>, General <a href="/wiki/Douglas_MacArthur" title="Douglas MacArthur">Douglas MacArthur</a> called on United Nations forces, including U.S. Marines, to make an amphibious landing at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Inchon" title="Battle of Inchon">Inchon</a>. The successful landing resulted in the collapse of North Korean lines and the pursuit of North Korean forces north near the <a href="/wiki/Yalu_River" title="Yalu River">Yalu River</a> until the entrance of the People's Republic of China into the war. Chinese troops surrounded, surprised and overwhelmed the overextended and outnumbered American forces. The U.S. Army's X Corps, which included the <a href="/wiki/1st_Marine_Division_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="1st Marine Division (United States)">1st Marine Division</a> and the Army's 7th Infantry Division, regrouped and inflicted heavy casualties during their fighting withdrawal to the coast, known as the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Chosin_Reservoir" title="Battle of Chosin Reservoir">Battle of Chosin Reservoir</a>.
</p><p>The fighting calmed after the Battle of the Chosin Reservoir, but late in March 1953 the relative quiet of the war was broken when the People's Liberation Army launched a massive offensive on three outposts manned by the 5th Marine Regiment. These outposts were codenamed "Reno", "Vegas", and "Carson". The campaign was collectively known as the Nevada Cities Campaign. There was brutal fighting on Reno hill, which was eventually captured by the Chinese. Although Reno was lost, the 5th Marines held both Vegas and Carson through the rest of the campaign. In this one campaign, the Marines suffered approximately 1,000 casualties, and might have suffered much more without the U.S. Army's <a href="/wiki/Task_Force_Faith" title="Task Force Faith">Task Force Faith</a>. Marines would continue a battle of attrition around the <a href="/wiki/38th_parallel_north" title="38th parallel north">38th Parallel</a> until the 1953 armistice.<sup id="cite_ref-Fehrenbach_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fehrenbach-70">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Korean War saw the Corps expand from 75,000 regulars to a force of 261,000 Marines, mostly reservists. 30,544 Marines were killed or wounded during the war and 42 were awarded the Medal of Honor.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Vietnam_War">Vietnam War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Vietnam War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Marines_in_Operation_Allen_Brook_(Vietnam_War)_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/U.S._Marines_in_Operation_Allen_Brook_%28Vietnam_War%29_001.jpg/220px-U.S._Marines_in_Operation_Allen_Brook_%28Vietnam_War%29_001.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/U.S._Marines_in_Operation_Allen_Brook_%28Vietnam_War%29_001.jpg/330px-U.S._Marines_in_Operation_Allen_Brook_%28Vietnam_War%29_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/U.S._Marines_in_Operation_Allen_Brook_%28Vietnam_War%29_001.jpg/440px-U.S._Marines_in_Operation_Allen_Brook_%28Vietnam_War%29_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="673" data-file-height="518" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Marines_in_Operation_Allen_Brook_(Vietnam_War)_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. Marines of "G" Company, <a href="/wiki/2nd_Battalion,_7th_Marines" title="2nd Battalion, 7th Marines">2nd Battalion, 7th Marines</a> in action during <a href="/wiki/Operation_Allen_Brook" title="Operation Allen Brook">Operation Allen Brook</a> in South Vietnam, 1968</div></div></div>
<p>The Marine Corps served in the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">Vietnam War</a> taking part in such battles as the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Hue" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Hue">Battle of Hue</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Khe_Sanh" title="Battle of Khe Sanh">Battle of Khe Sanh</a> in 1968. Individuals from the USMC generally operated in the Northern I Corps Regions of <a href="/wiki/South_Vietnam" title="South Vietnam">South Vietnam</a>. While there, they were constantly engaged in a <a href="/wiki/Guerrilla_warfare" title="Guerrilla warfare">guerrilla war</a> against the <a href="/wiki/Viet_Cong" title="Viet Cong">Viet Cong</a>, along with an intermittent conventional war against the <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_People%27s_Army" class="mw-redirect" title="Vietnam People&#39;s Army">North Vietnamese Army</a> (NVA). Portions of the Corps were responsible for the less-known <a href="/wiki/Combined_Action_Program" title="Combined Action Program">Combined Action Program</a> (CAP) that implemented unconventional techniques for <a href="/wiki/Counter-insurgency" title="Counter-insurgency">counter-insurgency</a> and worked as military advisers to the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Vietnam_Marine_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Vietnam Marine Corps">Republic of Vietnam Marine Corps</a>. Marines were withdrawn in 1971, and returned briefly in 1975 to evacuate <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh_City" title="Ho Chi Minh City">Saigon</a> and attempt a rescue of the crew of the <a href="/wiki/Mayag%C3%BCez_incident" class="mw-redirect" title="Mayagüez incident">Mayagüez</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Millet_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Millet-72">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Vietnam was the longest war for Marines; by its end, 13,091<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CasualtiesTheWall_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CasualtiesTheWall-74">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> had been killed in action, 51,392 had been wounded, and 57 Medals of Honor had been awarded.<sup id="cite_ref-CasualtiesUSN_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CasualtiesUSN-75">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-USMC-MOH_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USMC-MOH-76">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> Due to policies concerning rotation, more Marines were deployed for service during Vietnam than World War II.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>While recovering from Vietnam, the Corps hit a detrimental low point in its service history caused by <a href="/wiki/Court-martial" title="Court-martial">courts-martial</a> and non-judicial punishments related partially to increased <a href="/wiki/Desertion" title="Desertion">unauthorized absences and desertions</a> during the war. Overhauling of the Corps began in the late 1970s, discharging the most delinquent, and once quality of new recruits improved, the Corps focused on reforming the NCO Corps, a vital functioning part of its forces.<sup id="cite_ref-Warren_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Warren-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Interim:_Vietnam_War_to_the_War_on_Terror">Interim: Vietnam War to the War on Terror</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Interim: Vietnam War to the War on Terror">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Beirut_Memorial_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Beirut_Memorial_1.jpg/220px-Beirut_Memorial_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8e/Beirut_Memorial_1.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Beirut_Memorial_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Beirut Memorial at <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Base_Camp_Lejeune" title="Marine Corps Base Camp Lejeune">Marine Corps Base Camp Lejeune</a></div></div></div>
<p>After the Vietnam War, the U.S. Marines resumed their expeditionary role, participating in the failed 1980 Iran hostage rescue attempt <a href="/wiki/Operation_Eagle_Claw" title="Operation Eagle Claw">Operation Eagle Claw</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of Grenada">invasion of Grenada</a> (Operation Urgent Fury) and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_invasion_of_Panama" title="United States invasion of Panama">invasion of Panama</a> (Operation Just Cause). On 23 October 1983, the Marine headquarters building in <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">Beirut</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">Lebanon</a>, was <a href="/wiki/1983_Beirut_barracks_bombing" class="mw-redirect" title="1983 Beirut barracks bombing">bombed</a>, causing the highest peacetime losses to the Corps in its history (220 Marines and 21 other service members were killed) and leading to the American withdrawal from the country. The year 1990 saw Marines of the <a href="/wiki/Operation_Sharp_Edge" title="Operation Sharp Edge">Joint Task Force Sharp Edge</a> save thousands of lives by evacuating British, French and American nationals from the violence of the <a href="/wiki/First_Liberian_Civil_War" title="First Liberian Civil War">Liberian Civil War</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:3-3_India_CO_Desert_Storm.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/3-3_India_CO_Desert_Storm.jpg/220px-3-3_India_CO_Desert_Storm.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/3-3_India_CO_Desert_Storm.jpg/330px-3-3_India_CO_Desert_Storm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/3-3_India_CO_Desert_Storm.jpg/440px-3-3_India_CO_Desert_Storm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="414" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:3-3_India_CO_Desert_Storm.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. Marines from <a href="/wiki/3rd_Battalion,_3rd_Marines" title="3rd Battalion, 3rd Marines">3rd Battalion, 3rd Marines</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Desert_Storm" class="mw-redirect" title="Desert Storm">Desert Storm</a> deployment in 1990–1991</div></div></div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_War" title="Gulf War">Persian Gulf War</a> of 1990 to 1991, Marine task forces formed for Operation Desert Shield, and later liberated <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>, along with Coalition forces, in Operation Desert Storm.<sup id="cite_ref-Simmons_41-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Simmons-41">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Marines participated in combat operations in Somalia (1992–1995) during Operations <a href="/wiki/Operation_Restore_Hope" class="mw-redirect" title="Operation Restore Hope">Restore Hope</a>, Restore Hope II, and <a href="/wiki/Operation_United_Shield" title="Operation United Shield">United Shield</a> to provide humanitarian relief.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, Marines took part in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Silver_Wake" title="Operation Silver Wake">Operation Silver Wake</a>, the evacuation of American citizens from the US Embassy in Tirana, Albania.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_War_on_Terrorism">Global War on Terrorism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Global War on Terrorism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marines_in_Saddams_palace_DM-SD-04-12222.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Color photograph of three U.S. Marines entering a partially destroyed palace" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Marines_in_Saddams_palace_DM-SD-04-12222.jpg/220px-Marines_in_Saddams_palace_DM-SD-04-12222.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Marines_in_Saddams_palace_DM-SD-04-12222.jpg/330px-Marines_in_Saddams_palace_DM-SD-04-12222.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/Marines_in_Saddams_palace_DM-SD-04-12222.jpg/440px-Marines_in_Saddams_palace_DM-SD-04-12222.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1720" data-file-height="1160" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marines_in_Saddams_palace_DM-SD-04-12222.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. Marines from <a href="/wiki/1st_Battalion,_7th_Marines" title="1st Battalion, 7th Marines">1st Battalion, 7th Marines</a> enter a palace in <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a> in April 2003.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:3rd_Battalion_3rd_Marines_dawn_patrol.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/3rd_Battalion_3rd_Marines_dawn_patrol.jpg/220px-3rd_Battalion_3rd_Marines_dawn_patrol.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/3rd_Battalion_3rd_Marines_dawn_patrol.jpg/330px-3rd_Battalion_3rd_Marines_dawn_patrol.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/3rd_Battalion_3rd_Marines_dawn_patrol.jpg/440px-3rd_Battalion_3rd_Marines_dawn_patrol.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1400" data-file-height="997" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:3rd_Battalion_3rd_Marines_dawn_patrol.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. Marines conducting a dawn patrol in Afghanistan's <a href="/wiki/Nawa-I-Barakzayi_District" title="Nawa-I-Barakzayi District">Nawa District</a>, Helmand Province (May 2010)</div></div></div>
<p>Following the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">attacks on 11 September 2001</a>, President <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">George W. Bush</a> announced the <a href="/wiki/Global_War_on_Terrorism" class="mw-redirect" title="Global War on Terrorism">Global War on Terrorism</a>. The stated objective of the Global War on Terror is "the defeat of <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">Al-Qaeda</a>, other terrorist groups and any nation that supports or harbors terrorists".<sup id="cite_ref-WhiteHouse_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WhiteHouse-79">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> Since then, the Marine Corps, alongside the other military services, has engaged in global operations around the world in support of that mission.
</p><p>In spring 2009, President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>'s goal of reducing spending in the Defense Department was led by Secretary <a href="/wiki/Robert_Gates" title="Robert Gates">Robert Gates</a> in a series of budget cuts that did not significantly change the Corps's budget and programs, cutting only the <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Martin_VH-71_Kestrel" title="Lockheed Martin VH-71 Kestrel">VH-71 Kestrel</a> and resetting the <a href="/wiki/VXX" title="VXX">VXX</a> program.<sup id="cite_ref-cut_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cut-80">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NYTimes_Spending_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYTimes_Spending-81">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-WP_Spending_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WP_Spending-82">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> However, the <a href="/wiki/National_Commission_on_Fiscal_Responsibility_and_Reform" title="National Commission on Fiscal Responsibility and Reform">National Commission on Fiscal Responsibility and Reform</a> singled the Corps out for the brunt of a series of recommended cuts in late 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> In light of <a href="/wiki/Budget_sequestration_in_2013" class="mw-redirect" title="Budget sequestration in 2013">budget sequestration in 2013</a>, General Amos set a goal of a force of 174,000 Marines.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> He testified that this was the minimum number that would allow for an effective response to even a single contingency operation, but it would reduce the peacetime ratio of time at home bases to time deployed down to a historical low level.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Afghanistan_Campaign_.28Operation_Enduring_Freedom-Afghanistan.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Afghanistan_Campaign_(Operation_Enduring_Freedom-Afghanistan)">Afghanistan Campaign (Operation Enduring Freedom-Afghanistan)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Afghanistan Campaign (Operation Enduring Freedom-Afghanistan)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:1st_platoon,_Alpha_Company,_1st_Battalion,_9th_Marine_Regiment,_24th_MEU,_Djibouti,_2010.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/1st_platoon%2C_Alpha_Company%2C_1st_Battalion%2C_9th_Marine_Regiment%2C_24th_MEU%2C_Djibouti%2C_2010.jpg/220px-1st_platoon%2C_Alpha_Company%2C_1st_Battalion%2C_9th_Marine_Regiment%2C_24th_MEU%2C_Djibouti%2C_2010.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/1st_platoon%2C_Alpha_Company%2C_1st_Battalion%2C_9th_Marine_Regiment%2C_24th_MEU%2C_Djibouti%2C_2010.jpg/330px-1st_platoon%2C_Alpha_Company%2C_1st_Battalion%2C_9th_Marine_Regiment%2C_24th_MEU%2C_Djibouti%2C_2010.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/1st_platoon%2C_Alpha_Company%2C_1st_Battalion%2C_9th_Marine_Regiment%2C_24th_MEU%2C_Djibouti%2C_2010.jpg/440px-1st_platoon%2C_Alpha_Company%2C_1st_Battalion%2C_9th_Marine_Regiment%2C_24th_MEU%2C_Djibouti%2C_2010.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2430" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:1st_platoon,_Alpha_Company,_1st_Battalion,_9th_Marine_Regiment,_24th_MEU,_Djibouti,_2010.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>U.S. Marines dismounting from an <a href="/wiki/Assault_Amphibious_Vehicle" title="Assault Amphibious Vehicle">Assault Amphibious Vehicle</a> in Djibouti</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Operation_Moshtarak.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Operation_Moshtarak.jpg/220px-Operation_Moshtarak.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Operation_Moshtarak.jpg/330px-Operation_Moshtarak.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cc/Operation_Moshtarak.jpg 2x" data-file-width="346" data-file-height="358" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Operation_Moshtarak.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Marine <a href="/wiki/Corporal" title="Corporal">Corporal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lance_Corporal" class="mw-redirect" title="Lance Corporal">Lance Corporal</a> of <a href="/wiki/3rd_Battalion_6th_Marines" class="mw-redirect" title="3rd Battalion 6th Marines">3rd Battalion, 6th Marines</a> engaging the enemy during <a href="/wiki/Operation_Moshtarak" title="Operation Moshtarak">Operation Moshtarak</a> in Afghanistan's <a href="/wiki/Helmand_Province" title="Helmand Province">Helmand Province</a></div></div></div>
<p>Marines and other American forces began staging in Pakistan and Uzbekistan on the border of Afghanistan as early as October 2001 in preparation for <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001–present)">Operation Enduring Freedom</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/15th_Marine_Expeditionary_Unit" title="15th Marine Expeditionary Unit">15th</a> and <a href="/wiki/26th_Marine_Expeditionary_Unit" title="26th Marine Expeditionary Unit">26th Marine Expeditionary Units</a> were some of the first conventional forces into Afghanistan in support of Operation Enduring Freedom in November 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-IHT_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IHT-87">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Since then, Marine battalions and squadrons have been rotating through, engaging <a href="/wiki/Taliban" title="Taliban">Taliban</a> and <a href="/wiki/Al-Qaeda" title="Al-Qaeda">Al-Qaeda</a> forces. Marines of the <a href="/wiki/24th_Marine_Expeditionary_Unit" title="24th Marine Expeditionary Unit">24th Marine Expeditionary Unit</a> flooded into the Taliban-held town of <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Garmsir" title="Battle of Garmsir">Garmsir</a> on 29 April 2008, in <a href="/wiki/Helmand_Province_campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="Helmand Province campaign">Helmand Province</a>, in the first major American operation in the region in years.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> In June 2009, 7,000 Marines with the <a href="/wiki/2nd_Marine_Expeditionary_Brigade_(United_States)" title="2nd Marine Expeditionary Brigade (United States)">2nd Marine Expeditionary Brigade</a> deployed to Afghanistan in an effort to improve security,<sup id="cite_ref-CBS_MEB-A_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CBS_MEB-A-89">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> and began <a href="/wiki/Operation_Strike_of_the_Sword" title="Operation Strike of the Sword">Operation Strike of the Sword</a> the next month. In February 2010, the 2nd Marine Expeditionary Brigade launched the largest offensive of the Afghan Campaign since 2001, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Marjah" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Marjah">Battle of Marjah</a>, to clear the Taliban from their key stronghold in Helmand Province.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> After Marjah, Marines progressed north up the Helmand River and cleared the towns of Kajahki and Sangin. Marines remained in Helmand Province until 2014.
</p>
<h4><span id="Iraq_Campaign_.28Operations_Iraqi_Freedom.2C_New_Dawn.2C_Inherent_Resolve.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Iraq_Campaign_(Operations_Iraqi_Freedom,_New_Dawn,_Inherent_Resolve)">Iraq Campaign (Operations Iraqi Freedom, New Dawn, Inherent Resolve)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Iraq Campaign (Operations Iraqi Freedom, New Dawn, Inherent Resolve)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
