<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Marines_with_3rd_Battalion,_4th_Marines.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/U.S._Marines_with_3rd_Battalion%2C_4th_Marines.jpg/220px-U.S._Marines_with_3rd_Battalion%2C_4th_Marines.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/U.S._Marines_with_3rd_Battalion%2C_4th_Marines.jpg/330px-U.S._Marines_with_3rd_Battalion%2C_4th_Marines.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/U.S._Marines_with_3rd_Battalion%2C_4th_Marines.jpg/440px-U.S._Marines_with_3rd_Battalion%2C_4th_Marines.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="667" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Marines_with_3rd_Battalion,_4th_Marines.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/3rd_Battalion,_4th_Marines" title="3rd Battalion, 4th Marines">3rd Battalion, 4th Marines</a> loading 120mm mortar rounds during <a href="/wiki/CJTF-OIR" class="mw-redirect" title="CJTF-OIR">Operation Inherent Resolve</a> in Syria, November 2018</div></div></div>
<p>U.S. Marines served in the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">Iraq War</a>, along with its sister services. The <a href="/wiki/I_Marine_Expeditionary_Force" title="I Marine Expeditionary Force">I Marine Expeditionary Force</a>, along with the U.S. Army's <a href="/wiki/3rd_Infantry_Division_(United_States)" title="3rd Infantry Division (United States)">3rd Infantry Division</a>, spearheaded the <a href="/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" title="2003 invasion of Iraq">2003 invasion of Iraq</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> The Marines left Iraq in the summer of 2003, but returned in the beginning of 2004. They were given <a href="/wiki/Multi-National_Forces_West" class="mw-redirect" title="Multi-National Forces West">responsibility</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War_in_Anbar_Province" class="mw-redirect" title="Iraq War in Anbar Province">Al Anbar Province</a>, the large desert region to the west of <a href="/wiki/Baghdad" title="Baghdad">Baghdad</a>. During this occupation, the Marines lead assaults on the city of <a href="/wiki/Fallujah" title="Fallujah">Fallujah</a> in April (<a href="/wiki/First_Battle_of_Fallujah" title="First Battle of Fallujah">Operation Vigilant Resolve</a>) and November 2004 (<a href="/wiki/Second_Battle_of_Fallujah" title="Second Battle of Fallujah">Operation Phantom Fury</a>) and saw intense fighting in such places as <a href="/wiki/Ramadi" title="Ramadi">Ramadi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Al-Qa%27im_(town)" title="Al-Qa&#39;im (town)">Al-Qa'im</a> and <a href="/wiki/H%C4%ABt" title="Hīt">Hīt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Their time in Iraq has courted controversy with the <a href="/wiki/Haditha_killings" class="mw-redirect" title="Haditha killings">Haditha killings</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Hamdania_incident" title="Hamdania incident">Hamdania incident</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Post_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Post-94">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Sons_of_Iraq" title="Sons of Iraq">Anbar Awakening</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War_troop_surge_of_2007" title="Iraq War troop surge of 2007">2007 surge</a> reduced levels of violence. The Marine Corps officially ended its role in Iraq on 23 January 2010 when they handed over responsibility for Al Anbar Province to the U.S. Army.<sup id="cite_ref-Detroit_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Detroit-95">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-outofiraq?_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-outofiraq?-96">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> U.S. Marines would ultimately <a href="/wiki/2014_American_intervention_in_Iraq" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 American intervention in Iraq">return to Iraq in the summer of 2014</a>, in response to growing violence there.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Throughout the Global War on Terrorism, the U.S. Marines have supported operations in Africa to counter Islamic extremism and piracy in the Red Sea. In late 2002, <a href="/wiki/Combined_Joint_Task_Force_%E2%80%93_Horn_of_Africa" title="Combined Joint Task Force – Horn of Africa">Combined Joint Task Force – Horn of Africa</a> was stood up at <a href="/wiki/Camp_Lemonnier" title="Camp Lemonnier">Camp Lemonnier</a>, Djibouti to provide regional security.<sup id="cite_ref-CJTF-HOA2_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CJTF-HOA2-98">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> Despite transferring overall command to the Navy in 2006, the Marines continued to <a href="/wiki/Operation_Enduring_Freedom_%E2%80%93_Horn_of_Africa" title="Operation Enduring Freedom – Horn of Africa">operate</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Horn_of_Africa" title="Horn of Africa">Horn of Africa</a> into 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-USMC2_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USMC2-99">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Organization_of_the_United_States_Marine_Corps" title="Organization of the United States Marine Corps">Organization of the United States Marine Corps</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Department_of_the_Navy">Department of the Navy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Department of the Navy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Navy" title="United States Department of the Navy">Department of the Navy</a>, led by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Navy" title="United States Secretary of the Navy">Secretary of the Navy</a>, is a military department of the cabinet-level <a href="/wiki/U.S._Department_of_Defense" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. Department of Defense">U.S. Department of Defense</a> that oversees the Marine Corps and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">Navy</a>. The most senior Marine officer is the <a href="/wiki/Commandant_of_the_Marine_Corps" title="Commandant of the Marine Corps">Commandant</a> (unless a Marine officer is the <a href="/wiki/Chairman_of_the_Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff" title="Chairman of the Joint Chiefs of Staff">Chairman of the Joint Chiefs</a> or <a href="/wiki/Vice_Chairman_of_the_Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff" title="Vice Chairman of the Joint Chiefs of Staff">Vice Chairman of the Joint Chiefs</a>), responsible to the Secretary of the Navy for organizing, recruiting, training, and equipping the Marine Corps so that its forces are ready for deployment under the operational command of the <a href="/wiki/Unified_Combatant_Command" class="mw-redirect" title="Unified Combatant Command">Combatant Commanders</a>. The Marine Corps is organized into four principal subdivisions: <a href="/wiki/Headquarters_Marine_Corps" title="Headquarters Marine Corps">Headquarters Marine Corps</a> (HQMC), the Operating Forces, the Supporting Establishment, and the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Forces_Reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine Forces Reserve">Marine Forces Reserve</a> (MARFORRES or USMCR).
</p>
<h3><span id="Headquarters_Marine_Corps_.28HQMC.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Headquarters_Marine_Corps_(HQMC)">Headquarters Marine Corps (HQMC)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Headquarters Marine Corps (HQMC)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Headquarters Marine Corps consists of the Commandant of the Marine Corps, the Assistant Commandant of the Marine Corps, the Director Marine Corps Staff, the several Deputy Commandants, the Sergeant Major of the Marine Corps, and various special staff officers and Marine Corps agency heads that report directly to either the Commandant or Assistant Commandant. HQMC is supported by the Headquarters and Service Battalion, USMC providing administrative, supply, logistics, training, and services support to the Commandant and his staff.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operating_Forces">Operating Forces</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Operating Forces">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Operating Forces are divided into three categories: Marine Corps Forces (MARFOR) assigned to unified combatant commands, viz., the <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Marine_Force" title="Fleet Marine Force">Fleet Marine Forces</a> (FMF), <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Security_Force_Regiment" title="Marine Corps Security Force Regiment">Security Forces</a> guarding high-risk naval installations, and <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Security_Guard" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine Corps Security Guard">Security Guard</a> detachments at <a href="/wiki/List_of_American_embassies" class="mw-redirect" title="List of American embassies">American embassies</a>. Under the "Forces for Unified Commands" memo, in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Unified_Command_Plan" class="mw-redirect" title="Unified Command Plan">Unified Command Plan</a> approved by the President, Marine Corps Forces are assigned to each of the <a href="/wiki/Unified_Combatant_Command" class="mw-redirect" title="Unified Combatant Command">Combatant Commands</a> at the discretion of the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Defense" title="United States Secretary of Defense">Secretary of Defense</a>. Since 1991, the Marine Corps has maintained component headquarters at each of the regional unified combatant commands.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Marine Corps Forces are divided into <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps_Forces_Command" title="United States Marine Corps Forces Command">Forces Command</a> (MARFORCOM) and <a href="/wiki/Marine_Forces_Pacific" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine Forces Pacific">Pacific Command</a> (MARFORPAC), each headed by a <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_General_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lieutenant General (United States)">lieutenant general</a> dual-posted as the commanding general of either <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Marine_Force,_Atlantic" title="Fleet Marine Force, Atlantic">FMF Atlantic (FMFLANT)</a> or <a href="/wiki/Fleet_Marine_Force,_Pacific" title="Fleet Marine Force, Pacific">FMF Pacific (FMFPAC)</a>, respectively. MARFORCOM/FMFLANT has operational control of the <a href="/wiki/II_Marine_Expeditionary_Force" title="II Marine Expeditionary Force">II Marine Expeditionary Force</a>; MARFORPAC/FMFPAC has operational control of the <a href="/wiki/I_Marine_Expeditionary_Force" title="I Marine Expeditionary Force">I Marine Expeditionary Force</a> and <a href="/wiki/III_Marine_Expeditionary_Force" title="III Marine Expeditionary Force">III Marine Expeditionary Force</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ChenowethNihart_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChenowethNihart-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Marine_Air-Ground_Task_Force_.28MAGTF.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Marine_Air-Ground_Task_Force_(MAGTF)">Marine Air-Ground Task Force (MAGTF)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Marine Air-Ground Task Force (MAGTF)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Marine_Air-Ground_Task_Force" title="Marine Air-Ground Task Force">Marine Air-Ground Task Force</a></div>
<p>The basic framework for deployable Marine units is the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Air-Ground_Task_Force" title="Marine Air-Ground Task Force">Marine Air-Ground Task Force</a> (MAGTF), a flexible structure of varying size. A MAGTF integrates a <a href="/wiki/Ground_combat_element" title="Ground combat element">ground combat element</a> (GCE), an <a href="/wiki/Aviation_combat_element" title="Aviation combat element">aviation combat element</a> (ACE), and a <a href="/wiki/Logistics_combat_element" title="Logistics combat element">logistics combat element</a> (LCE) under a common <a href="/wiki/Command_element_(United_States_Marine_Corps)" title="Command element (United States Marine Corps)">command element</a> (CE), capable of operating independently or as part of a larger coalition. The MAGTF structure reflects a strong preference in the Corps towards self-sufficiency and a commitment to <a href="/wiki/Combined_arms" title="Combined arms">combined arms</a>, both essential assets to an <a href="/wiki/Expeditionary_warfare" title="Expeditionary warfare">expeditionary force</a>. The Marine Corps has a wariness and distrust of reliance on its sister services, and towards joint operations in general.<sup id="cite_ref-Warren_29-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Warren-29">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Supporting_Establishment">Supporting Establishment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Supporting Establishment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Supporting Establishment includes the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Combat_Development_Command" title="Marine Corps Combat Development Command">Combat Development Command</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Logistics_Command" title="Marine Corps Logistics Command">Logistics Command</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Systems_Command" title="Marine Corps Systems Command">Systems Command</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Recruiting_Command" title="Marine Corps Recruiting Command">Recruiting Command</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Installations_Command" title="Marine Corps Installations Command">Installations Command</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Band" title="United States Marine Band">Marine Band</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Drum_and_Bugle_Corps" title="United States Marine Drum and Bugle Corps">Marine Drum and Bugle Corps</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Marine_Corps_bases_and_stations">Marine Corps bases and stations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Marine Corps bases and stations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Marine_Corps_installations" title="List of United States Marine Corps installations">List of United States Marine Corps installations</a></div>
<p>The Marine Corps operates many major bases, 14 of which host operating forces, several support and training installations, as well as satellite facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-BGenWilliams_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BGenWilliams-101">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Marine Corps bases are concentrated around the locations of the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Expeditionary_Force" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine Expeditionary Force">Marine Expeditionary Forces</a>, though <a href="/wiki/Marine_Forces_Reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine Forces Reserve">reserve units</a> are scattered throughout the United States. The principal bases are <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Base_Camp_Pendleton" title="Marine Corps Base Camp Pendleton">Camp Pendleton</a> on the West Coast, home to <a href="/wiki/I_Marine_Expeditionary_Force" title="I Marine Expeditionary Force">I MEF</a>; <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Base_Camp_Lejeune" title="Marine Corps Base Camp Lejeune">Camp Lejeune</a> on the East Coast, home to <a href="/wiki/II_Marine_Expeditionary_Force" title="II Marine Expeditionary Force">II MEF</a>; and <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Base_Camp_Smedley_D._Butler" title="Marine Corps Base Camp Smedley D. Butler">Camp Butler</a> in <a href="/wiki/Okinawa_Prefecture" title="Okinawa Prefecture">Okinawa, Japan</a>, home to <a href="/wiki/III_Marine_Expeditionary_Force" title="III Marine Expeditionary Force">III MEF</a>.
</p><p>Other important bases include air stations, recruit depots, logistics bases, and training commands. <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Air_Ground_Combat_Center_Twentynine_Palms" title="Marine Corps Air Ground Combat Center Twentynine Palms">Marine Corps Air Ground Combat Center Twentynine Palms</a> in California is the Marine Corps's largest base and home to the Corps's most complex, combined-arms, live-fire training. <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Base_Quantico" title="Marine Corps Base Quantico">Marine Corps Base Quantico</a> in <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a> is home to <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Combat_Development_Command" title="Marine Corps Combat Development Command">Marine Corps Combat Development Command</a>, and nicknamed the "Crossroads of the Marine Corps".<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Marine Corps maintains a significant presence in the <a href="/wiki/National_Capital_Region_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="National Capital Region (United States)">National Capital Region</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Headquarters_Marine_Corps" title="Headquarters Marine Corps">Headquarters Marine Corps</a> scattered amongst <a href="/wiki/The_Pentagon" title="The Pentagon">the Pentagon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Henderson_Hall_(Arlington,_Virginia)" title="Henderson Hall (Arlington, Virginia)">Henderson Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Washington_Navy_Yard" title="Washington Navy Yard">Washington Navy Yard</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Marine_Barracks,_Washington,_D.C." title="Marine Barracks, Washington, D.C.">Marine Barracks, Washington, D.C.</a> Additionally, Marines operate <a href="/wiki/Detachment_(military)" title="Detachment (military)">detachments</a> at many installations owned by other branches, to better share resources, such as specialty schools. Marines are also present at, and operate many, forward bases during expeditionary operations.
</p>
<h3><span id="Marine_Forces_Reserve_.28MARFORRES.2FUSMCR.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Marine_Forces_Reserve_(MARFORRES/USMCR)">Marine Forces Reserve (MARFORRES/USMCR)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Marine Forces Reserve (MARFORRES/USMCR)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Marine Forces Reserve consists of the Force Headquarters Group, 4th Marine Division, 4th Marine Aircraft Wing, and the 4th Marine Logistics Group. The MARFORRES/USMCR is capable of forming a 4th Marine Expeditionary Force (MEF) or reinforcing/augmenting active-duty forces.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_Operations">Special Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Special Operations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps_Forces_Special_Operations_Command" title="United States Marine Corps Forces Special Operations Command">United States Marine Corps Forces Special Operations Command</a></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Marine_Raider_Regiment" title="Marine Raider Regiment">Marine Raider Regiment</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps_Special_Operations_Capable_Forces" title="United States Marine Corps Special Operations Capable Forces">United States Marine Corps Special Operations Capable Forces</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MARSOC_are_shooting_with_M4_at_Washoe_Coutny_Reginal_Shooting_Facility.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/MARSOC_are_shooting_with_M4_at_Washoe_Coutny_Reginal_Shooting_Facility.jpg/220px-MARSOC_are_shooting_with_M4_at_Washoe_Coutny_Reginal_Shooting_Facility.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/MARSOC_are_shooting_with_M4_at_Washoe_Coutny_Reginal_Shooting_Facility.jpg/330px-MARSOC_are_shooting_with_M4_at_Washoe_Coutny_Reginal_Shooting_Facility.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/MARSOC_are_shooting_with_M4_at_Washoe_Coutny_Reginal_Shooting_Facility.jpg/440px-MARSOC_are_shooting_with_M4_at_Washoe_Coutny_Reginal_Shooting_Facility.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="497" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MARSOC_are_shooting_with_M4_at_Washoe_Coutny_Reginal_Shooting_Facility.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marine Raiders conduct <a href="/wiki/Close_combat" title="Close combat">CQB</a> training</div></div></div>
<p>Marine Corps Forces Special Operations Command (MARSOC) includes: the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Raider_Regiment" title="Marine Raider Regiment">Marine Raider Regiment</a>, the Marine Raider Support Group, and the Marine Special Operations School. Both the Raider Regiment and the Raider Support Group consist of a headquarters company and three operations battalions. The Special Operations School conducts screening, assessment, selection, training and development functions for MARSOC units.
</p><p>Marine Corps Special Operations Capable forces include: <a href="/wiki/Air_Naval_Gunfire_Liaison_Company" class="mw-redirect" title="Air Naval Gunfire Liaison Company">Air Naval Gunfire Liaison Companies</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Chemical_Biological_Incident_Response_Force" title="Chemical Biological Incident Response Force">Chemical Biological Incident Response Force</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps_Reconnaissance_Battalions" title="United States Marine Corps Reconnaissance Battalions">Marine Division Reconnaissance Battalions</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps_Force_Reconnaissance" title="United States Marine Corps Force Reconnaissance">Force Reconnaissance Companies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Special_Purpose_Force" title="Maritime Special Purpose Force">Maritime Special Purpose Force</a>, and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps_Special_Operations_Capable_Forces#Special_Reaction_Teams" title="United States Marine Corps Special Operations Capable Forces">Special Reaction Teams</a>. Additionally, all deployed <a href="/wiki/Marine_Expeditionary_Unit" class="mw-redirect" title="Marine Expeditionary Unit">Marine Expeditionary Units</a> are certified as "<a href="/wiki/Special_Operations_Capable" class="mw-redirect" title="Special Operations Capable">Special Operations Capable</a>", viz. "MEU(SOC)", however Special Operations Capable forces are not considered to be special operations forces.
</p><p>Although the notion of a Marine special operations forces contribution to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Special_Operations_Command" title="United States Special Operations Command">United States Special Operations Command</a> (USSOCOM) was considered as early as the founding of USSOCOM in the 1980s, it was resisted by the Marine Corps. Then-Commandant <a href="/wiki/Paul_X._Kelley" title="Paul X. Kelley">Paul X. Kelley</a> expressed the belief that Marines should only support Marines, and that the Corps should not fund a special operations capability that would not directly support Marine operations.<sup id="cite_ref-WThomasSmith_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WThomasSmith-104">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> However, much of the resistance from within the Corps dissipated when Marine leaders watched the Corps's 15th and 26th MEU(SOC)s "sit on the sidelines" during the very early stages of <a href="/wiki/Operation_Enduring_Freedom" title="Operation Enduring Freedom">Operation Enduring Freedom</a> while other special operations units from the Army, Navy, and Air Force actively engaged in operations in Afghanistan.<sup id="cite_ref-Priddy_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Priddy-105">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> After a three-year development period, the Corps agreed in 2006 to supply a 2,500-strong unit, Marine Forces Special Operations Command, which would answer directly to USSOCOM.<sup id="cite_ref-Bradley_Graham_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bradley_Graham-106">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personnel">Personnel</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Personnel">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_notable_United_States_Marines" class="mw-redirect" title="List of notable United States Marines">List of notable United States Marines</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_historically_notable_United_States_Marines" class="mw-redirect" title="List of historically notable United States Marines">List of historically notable United States Marines</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Leadership">Leadership</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Leadership">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r889293853/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:left;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:387px;max-width:387px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:127px;max-width:127px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Gen._David_H._Berger.jpg" class="image"><img alt="color photograph of Joseph F. Dunford, Jr." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Gen._David_H._Berger.jpg/125px-Gen._David_H._Berger.jpg" decoding="async" width="125" height="156" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Gen._David_H._Berger.jpg/188px-Gen._David_H._Berger.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Gen._David_H._Berger.jpg/250px-Gen._David_H._Berger.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="3000" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/David_H._Berger" title="David H. Berger">David Berger</a>, <br /><a href="/wiki/Commandant_of_the_Marine_Corps" title="Commandant of the Marine Corps">Commandant of the Marine Corps</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:127px;max-width:127px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:ACMC_2018_HiRes.jpg" class="image"><img alt="color photograph of John M. Paxton, Jr." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/ACMC_2018_HiRes.jpg/125px-ACMC_2018_HiRes.jpg" decoding="async" width="125" height="156" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/ACMC_2018_HiRes.jpg/188px-ACMC_2018_HiRes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/ACMC_2018_HiRes.jpg/250px-ACMC_2018_HiRes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2437" data-file-height="3046" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Gary_L._Thomas_(general)" title="Gary L. Thomas (general)">Gary L. Thomas</a>, <br /><a href="/wiki/Assistant_Commandant_of_the_Marine_Corps" title="Assistant Commandant of the Marine Corps">Assistant Commandant of the Marine Corps</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:127px;max-width:127px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:19th_Sergeant_Major_of_the_Marine_Corps_Troy_E._Black.jpg" class="image"><img alt="color photograph of Troy E. Black" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/19th_Sergeant_Major_of_the_Marine_Corps_Troy_E._Black.jpg/125px-19th_Sergeant_Major_of_the_Marine_Corps_Troy_E._Black.jpg" decoding="async" width="125" height="156" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/19th_Sergeant_Major_of_the_Marine_Corps_Troy_E._Black.jpg/188px-19th_Sergeant_Major_of_the_Marine_Corps_Troy_E._Black.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/19th_Sergeant_Major_of_the_Marine_Corps_Troy_E._Black.jpg/250px-19th_Sergeant_Major_of_the_Marine_Corps_Troy_E._Black.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1250" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption"><a href="/wiki/Troy_E._Black" title="Troy E. Black">Troy E. Black</a>, <br /><a href="/wiki/Sergeant_Major_of_the_Marine_Corps" title="Sergeant Major of the Marine Corps">Sergeant Major of the Marine Corps</a></div></div></div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Commandant_of_the_Marine_Corps" title="Commandant of the Marine Corps">Commandant of the Marine Corps</a> is the highest-ranking officer of the Marine Corps, unless a Marine is either the chairman or Vice Chairman of the Joint Chiefs. The Commandant has the <a href="/wiki/Title_10_of_the_United_States_Code" title="Title 10 of the United States Code">U.S. Code Title 10</a> responsibility to staff, train, and equip the Marine Corps and has no command authority. The Commandant is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Joint_Chiefs_of_Staff" title="Joint Chiefs of Staff">Joint Chiefs of Staff</a>, and reports to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_the_Navy" title="United States Secretary of the Navy">Secretary of the Navy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Assistant_Commandant_of_the_Marine_Corps" title="Assistant Commandant of the Marine Corps">Assistant Commandant of the Marine Corps</a> acts as the chief deputy to the Commandant. The <a href="/wiki/Sergeant_Major_of_the_Marine_Corps" title="Sergeant Major of the Marine Corps">Sergeant Major of the Marine Corps</a> is the senior enlisted Marine, and acts as an adviser to the Commandant. <a href="/wiki/Headquarters_Marine_Corps" title="Headquarters Marine Corps">Headquarters Marine Corps</a> comprises the rest of the Commandant's counsel and <a href="/wiki/Staff_(military)" title="Staff (military)">staff</a>, with deputy Commandants that oversee various aspects of the Corps assets and capabilities.
</p><p>The current and 38th Commandant is <a href="/wiki/David_H._Berger" title="David H. Berger">David Berger</a>, who assumed the position on 11 July 2019.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> The 35th and current Assistant Commandant is <a href="/wiki/Gary_L._Thomas_(general)" title="Gary L. Thomas (general)">Gary L. Thomas</a>, while the 18th and current Sergeant Major is <a href="/wiki/Ronald_L._Green" title="Ronald L. Green">Ronald L. Green</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Women">Women</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Women">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Women_in_the_United_States_Marines" title="Women in the United States Marines">Women in the United States Marines</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:First_three_female_Marines_graduate_Infantry_training_course_131121-M-JR212-076.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/First_three_female_Marines_graduate_Infantry_training_course_131121-M-JR212-076.jpg/220px-First_three_female_Marines_graduate_Infantry_training_course_131121-M-JR212-076.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/First_three_female_Marines_graduate_Infantry_training_course_131121-M-JR212-076.jpg/330px-First_three_female_Marines_graduate_Infantry_training_course_131121-M-JR212-076.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/First_three_female_Marines_graduate_Infantry_training_course_131121-M-JR212-076.jpg/440px-First_three_female_Marines_graduate_Infantry_training_course_131121-M-JR212-076.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5760" data-file-height="3840" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:First_three_female_Marines_graduate_Infantry_training_course_131121-M-JR212-076.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Two of the first female graduates of the School of Infantry-East's Infantry Training Battalion course, 2013</div></div></div>
<p>Women have served in the USMC since 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> In January 2017, three women joined an infantry battalion at Camp Lejune. Women had not served as infantry Marines prior to this.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, the Marines released a recruitment ad that focused on women for the first time.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> women make up about 7% of the force.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rank_structure">Rank structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Rank structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps_rank_insignia" title="United States Marine Corps rank insignia">United States Marine Corps rank insignia</a></div>
<p>As in the rest of the United States Armed Forces (excluding the Air Force, which does not currently appoint warrant officers), Marine Corps <a href="/wiki/Military_rank" title="Military rank">ranks</a> fall into one of three categories: <a href="/wiki/Officer_(armed_forces)" title="Officer (armed forces)">commissioned officer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warrant_Officer_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Warrant Officer (United States)">warrant officer</a>, and enlisted, in decreasing order of authority. To standardize compensation, each rank is assigned a <a href="/wiki/Pay_grade" title="Pay grade">pay grade</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Commissioned_officers">Commissioned officers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Commissioned officers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Commissioned officers are distinguished from other officers by their <a href="/wiki/Commission_(document)" title="Commission (document)">commission</a>, which is the formal written authority, issued in the name of the President of the United States, that confers the rank and authority of a Marine officer. Commissioned officers carry the "special trust and confidence" of the President of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Estes_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Estes-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Marine Corps commissioned officers are promoted based on an "up or out" system in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Defense_Officer_Personnel_Management_Act" title="Defense Officer Personnel Management Act">Defense Officer Personnel Management Act</a> of 1980.
</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Warrant_officers">Warrant officers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Warrant officers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Warrant_officer_(United_States)" title="Warrant officer (United States)">Warrant officer (United States)</a></div>
<p>Warrant officers are primarily former enlisted experts in a specific specialized field and provide leadership generally only within that speciality.
</p>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Enlisted">Enlisted</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Enlisted">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">November 2017</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Enlisted Marines in the pay grades E-1 to E-3 make up the bulk of the Corps's ranks, usually referred to simply as "Marines". Although they do not technically hold leadership ranks, the Corps's ethos stresses leadership among all Marines, and junior Marines are often assigned responsibility normally reserved for superiors. Those in the pay grades of E-4 and E-5 are <a href="/wiki/Non-commissioned_officer" title="Non-commissioned officer">non-commissioned officers</a> (NCOs). They primarily supervise junior Marines and act as a vital link with the higher command structure, ensuring that orders are carried out correctly. Marines E-6 and higher are Staff Non-Commissioned Officers (SNCOs), charged with supervising NCOs and acting as enlisted advisers to the command.
</p><p>The E-8 and E-9 levels have two and three ranks per pay grade, respectively, each with different responsibilities. The First Sergeant and Sergeant Major ranks are command-oriented, serving as the senior enlisted Marines in a unit, charged to assist the commanding officer in matters of discipline, administration and the morale and welfare of the unit. Master Sergeants and Master Gunnery Sergeants provide technical leadership as occupational specialists in their specific MOS. The <a href="/wiki/Sergeant_Major_of_the_Marine_Corps" title="Sergeant Major of the Marine Corps">Sergeant Major of the Marine Corps</a> also E-9, is a billet conferred on the senior enlisted Marine of the entire Marine Corps, personally selected by the Commandant. It is possible however for an enlisted Marine to hold a position senior to Sergeant Major of the Marine Corps which was the case from 2011 to 2015 with the appointment of Sergeant Major <a href="/wiki/Bryan_B._Battaglia" title="Bryan B. Battaglia">Bryan B. Battaglia</a> to the billet of <a href="/wiki/Senior_Enlisted_Advisor_to_the_Chairman" title="Senior Enlisted Advisor to the Chairman">Senior Enlisted Advisor to the Chairman</a>, who is the senior enlisted member of the United States military.
</p><p>Different forms of address can be found at <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps_rank_insignia" title="United States Marine Corps rank insignia">United States Marine Corps rank insignia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Marine_Corps_acronyms_and_expressions" title="List of United States Marine Corps acronyms and expressions">List of United States Marine Corps acronyms and expressions</a>.
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military_Occupational_Specialty">Military Occupational Specialty</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Military Occupational Specialty">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Military_Occupational_Specialty" class="mw-redirect" title="Military Occupational Specialty">Military Occupational Specialty</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Marine_Corps_MOS" title="List of United States Marine Corps MOS">List of United States Marine Corps MOS</a></div>
<p>The Military Occupational Specialty (MOS) is a system of job classification. Using a four digit code, it designates what field and specific occupation a Marine performs. Segregated between officer and enlisted, the MOS determines the staffing of a unit. Some MOSs change with rank to reflect supervisory positions, others are secondary and represent a temporary assignment outside of a Marine's normal duties or special skill.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marine-m16.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Marine-m16.jpg/220px-Marine-m16.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Marine-m16.jpg/330px-Marine-m16.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Marine-m16.jpg/440px-Marine-m16.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="667" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marine-m16.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marine recruits on a Squad Rush course</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_training">Initial training</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Initial training">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps_Recruit_Training" title="United States Marine Corps Recruit Training">United States Marine Corps Recruit Training</a> and <a href="/wiki/Officer_Candidates_School_(United_States_Marine_Corps)" title="Officer Candidates School (United States Marine Corps)">Officer Candidates School (United States Marine Corps)</a></div>
<p>Every year, over 2,000 new Marine officers are commissioned, and 38,000 recruits accepted and trained.<sup id="cite_ref-ChenowethNihart_35-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChenowethNihart-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> All new Marines, enlisted or officer, are <a href="/wiki/Military_recruitment" title="Military recruitment">recruited</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Recruiting_Command" title="Marine Corps Recruiting Command">Marine Corps Recruiting Command</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Commissioned officers are commissioned mainly through one of three sources: <a href="/wiki/Naval_Reserve_Officer_Training_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="Naval Reserve Officer Training Corps">Naval Reserve Officer Training Corps</a> (NROTC), <a href="/wiki/Officer_Candidates_School_(United_States_Marine_Corps)" title="Officer Candidates School (United States Marine Corps)">Officer Candidates School</a> (OCS), or the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">United States Naval Academy</a> (USNA). Following commissioning, all Marine commissioned officers, regardless of accession route or further training requirements, attend <a href="/wiki/The_Basic_School" title="The Basic School">The Basic School</a> (TBS) at <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Base_Quantico" title="Marine Corps Base Quantico">Marine Corps Base Quantico</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginia</a>. At TBS, second lieutenants, warrant officers, and selected foreign officers learn the art of <a href="/wiki/Infantry" title="Infantry">infantry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Combined_arms" title="Combined arms">combined arms</a> warfare.<sup id="cite_ref-Estes_23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Estes-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marine_recruits.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Marine_recruits.jpg/220px-Marine_recruits.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Marine_recruits.jpg/330px-Marine_recruits.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Marine_recruits.jpg/440px-Marine_recruits.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="667" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marine_recruits.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marine recruits at Marine Corps Recruit Depot San Diego</div></div></div>
<p>Enlisted Marines attend <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps_Recruit_Training" title="United States Marine Corps Recruit Training">recruit training</a>, known as <i><a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps_Recruit_Training" title="United States Marine Corps Recruit Training">boot camp</a></i>, at either <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Recruit_Depot_San_Diego" title="Marine Corps Recruit Depot San Diego">Marine Corps Recruit Depot San Diego</a> or <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Recruit_Depot_Parris_Island" title="Marine Corps Recruit Depot Parris Island">Marine Corps Recruit Depot Parris Island</a>. Historically, the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a> served as a dividing line that delineated who would be trained where, while more recently, a <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Recruiting_Command#Structure" title="Marine Corps Recruiting Command">district system</a> has ensured a more even distribution of male recruits between the two MCRD facilities. Females attend only the Parris Island depot as part of the segregated Fourth Recruit Training Battalion. All recruits must pass a fitness test to start training; those who fail receive individualized attention and training until the minimum standards are reached. Marine recruit training is the longest among the American military services; it is 13 weeks long including processing and out-processing.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> The U.S Army basic training is currently 10 weeks long, however this does not include processing and out-processing.
</p><p>Following recruit training, enlisted Marines then attend <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps_School_of_Infantry" title="United States Marine Corps School of Infantry">The School of Infantry</a> at <a href="/wiki/Camp_Geiger" title="Camp Geiger">Camp Geiger</a> or <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Base_Camp_Pendleton" title="Marine Corps Base Camp Pendleton">Camp Pendleton</a>. Infantry Marines begin their combat training, which varies in length, immediately with the Infantry Training Battalion (ITB). Marines in all other MOSs other than infantry train for 29 days in Marine Combat Training (MCT), learning common infantry skills, before continuing on to their MOS schools, which vary in length.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Uniforms">Uniforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Uniforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Uniforms_of_the_United_States_Marine_Corps" title="Uniforms of the United States Marine Corps">Uniforms of the United States Marine Corps</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marine_dress_blues.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Marine_dress_blues.jpg/170px-Marine_dress_blues.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Marine_dress_blues.jpg/255px-Marine_dress_blues.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Marine_dress_blues.jpg/340px-Marine_dress_blues.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marine_dress_blues.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marine in "Dress Blues"</div></div></div>
<p>The Marine Corps has the most stable and most recognizable uniforms in the American military; the Dress Blues dates back to the early 19th century<sup id="cite_ref-ChenowethNihart_35-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChenowethNihart-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> and the service uniform to the early 20th century. Only a handful of skills (parachutist, air crew, explosive ordnance disposal, etc.) warrant <a href="/wiki/Badges_of_the_United_States_Marine_Corps" title="Badges of the United States Marine Corps">distinguishing badges</a>, and rank insignia is not worn on uniform headgear (with the exception of an officer's garrison service cover). While other servicemembers commonly identify with a sub-group as much as or more than their service (<a href="/wiki/Ranger_tab" title="Ranger tab">Ranger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Submarine_Warfare_insignia" title="Submarine Warfare insignia">submariner</a>, aircrew, etc.), Marine uniforms do not reflect such division.
</p><p>Marines have four main uniforms: Dress, Service, Utility, and Physical Training (PT). These uniforms have a few minor, but very distinct, variations from enlisted personnel to commissioned and non-commissioned officers. The Marine Corps <b><a href="/wiki/Dress_uniform" class="mw-redirect" title="Dress uniform">Dress uniform</a></b> is the most elaborate, worn for formal or ceremonial occasions. There are four different forms of the Dress uniform. The variations of the dress uniforms are known as "Alphas", "Bravos", "Charlies", or "Deltas". The most common being the "Blue Dress Alphas or Bravos", called "Dress Blues" or simply "Blues". It is most often seen in recruiting advertisements and is equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Black_tie" title="Black tie">black tie</a>. There is a "Blue-White" Dress for summer, and <a href="/wiki/Mess_dress" class="mw-redirect" title="Mess dress">Evening Dress</a> for formal (<a href="/wiki/White_tie" title="White tie">white tie</a>) occasions. Versions with a khaki shirt in lieu of the coat (Blue Dress Charlie/Delta) are worn as a daily working uniform by Marine recruiters and NROTC staff.<sup id="cite_ref-uniform_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uniform-118">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <b>Service Uniform</b> was once the prescribed daily work attire in garrison; however, it has been largely superseded in this role by the utility uniform. Consisting of olive green and khaki colors, it is commonly referred to as "Greens". It is roughly equivalent in function and composition to a <a href="/wiki/Suit_(clothing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Suit (clothing)">business suit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-uniform_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uniform-118">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <b>Utility Uniform</b>, currently the <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Combat_Utility_Uniform" title="Marine Corps Combat Utility Uniform">Marine Corps Combat Utility Uniform</a>, is a camouflage uniform intended for wear in the field or for dirty work in garrison, though it has been standardized for regular duty. It is rendered in <a href="/wiki/MARPAT" title="MARPAT">MARPAT</a> pixelated <a href="/wiki/Camouflage" title="Camouflage">camouflage</a> that breaks up the wearer's shape. In garrison, the woodland and desert uniforms are worn depending on the Marine's duty station.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup> Marines consider the utilities a working uniform and do not permit their wear off-base, except in transit to and from their place of duty and in the event of an emergency.<sup id="cite_ref-uniform_118-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uniform-118">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_the_United_States_Marine_Corps" title="Culture of the United States Marine Corps">Culture of the United States Marine Corps</a></div>
<p>As in any military organization, the official and unofficial traditions of the Marine Corps serve to reinforce camaraderie and set the service apart from others. The Corps's embrace of its rich culture and history is cited as a reason for its high <i>esprit de corps</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Estes_23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Estes-23">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flags,_USMC.png" class="image"><img alt="color artwork of an Eagle, Globe, and Anchor over crossed American and Marine flags" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Flags%2C_USMC.png/220px-Flags%2C_USMC.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="115" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Flags%2C_USMC.png/330px-Flags%2C_USMC.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6e/Flags%2C_USMC.png 2x" data-file-width="422" data-file-height="221" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flags,_USMC.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eagle, Globe and Anchor along with the U.S. flag, the Marine Corps flag and the Commandant's flag</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Official_traditions_and_customs">Official traditions and customs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Official traditions and customs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table role="presentation" class="mbox-small noprint" style="background-color:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;color:#000;">
<tbody><tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" decoding="async" width="50" height="50" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="160" data-file-height="160" /></div></div></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em"><div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:John_Philip_Sousa_-_U.S._Marine_Band_-_Semper_Fidelis_March.ogg" title="File:John Philip Sousa - U.S. Marine Band - Semper Fidelis March.ogg">Semper Fidelis March</a></div>
<div><div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio id="mwe_player_4" controls="" preload="none" style="width:220px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="255.21632653061" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="John_Philip_Sousa_-_U.S._Marine_Band_-_Semper_Fidelis_March.ogg" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/ff/John_Philip_Sousa_-_U.S._Marine_Band_-_Semper_Fidelis_March.ogg" type="audio/ogg; codecs=&quot;vorbis&quot;" data-title="Original Ogg file (75 kbps)" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="75002" /><source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/f/ff/John_Philip_Sousa_-_U.S._Marine_Band_-_Semper_Fidelis_March.ogg/John_Philip_Sousa_-_U.S._Marine_Band_-_Semper_Fidelis_March.ogg.mp3" type="audio/mpeg" data-title="MP3" data-shorttitle="MP3" data-transcodekey="mp3" data-width="0" data-height="0" data-bandwidth="127416" /></audio></div></div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0"><a href="/wiki/John_Philip_Sousa" title="John Philip Sousa">John Philip Sousa</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Semper_Fidelis_(march)" title="Semper Fidelis (march)">Semper Fidelis March</a>", the official march of the U.S. Marine Corps. Performed by the U.S. Marine Band in June 1909.</div></div></td></tr>
<tr><td colspan="2" class="mbox-text" style="line-height:1.1em"><hr /><i class="selfreference">Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Help:Media" title="Help:Media">media help</a>.</i></td></tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Marines%27_Hymn" title="Marines&#39; Hymn">Marines' Hymn</a></i> dates back to the 19th century and is the oldest official song in the United States armed forces. The Marine motto <i><a href="/wiki/Semper_Fidelis" class="mw-redirect" title="Semper Fidelis">Semper Fidelis</a></i> means <i>Always Faithful</i> in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a>, often appearing as <i>Semper Fi</i>; also the name of the <a href="/wiki/Semper_Fidelis_(march)" title="Semper Fidelis (march)">official march of the Corps</a>, composed by <a href="/wiki/John_Philip_Sousa" title="John Philip Sousa">John Philip Sousa</a>. The mottos <i>"Fortitudine"</i> (With Fortitude); <i>By Sea and by Land</i>, a translation of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Marines" title="Royal Marines">Royal Marines</a>' <i>Per Mare, Per Terram</i>; and <i>To the Shores of Tripoli</i> were used until 1868.<sup id="cite_ref-Customs_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Customs-120">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Marine Corps emblem</i> is the <a href="/wiki/Eagle,_Globe,_and_Anchor" title="Eagle, Globe, and Anchor">Eagle, Globe, and Anchor</a>, sometimes abbreviated "EGA", adopted in 1868.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> The Marine Corps seal includes the emblem, also is found on the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_United_States_Marine_Corps" title="Flag of the United States Marine Corps">flag of the United States Marine Corps</a>, and establishes scarlet and gold as the official colors.<sup id="cite_ref-Customs_EmblemSeal_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Customs_EmblemSeal-122">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Two styles of swords are worn by Marines: the officers' <a href="/wiki/Mameluke_Sword" class="mw-redirect" title="Mameluke Sword">Mameluke Sword</a>, similar to the Persian <a href="/wiki/Shamshir" title="Shamshir">shamshir</a> presented to Lt. <a href="/wiki/Presley_O%27Bannon" title="Presley O&#39;Bannon">Presley O'Bannon</a> after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Derna" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Derna">Battle of Derna</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps_noncommissioned_officer%27s_sword" title="United States Marine Corps noncommissioned officer&#39;s sword">Marine NCO sword</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ChenowethNihart_35-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ChenowethNihart-35">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps_birthday_ball" class="mw-redirect" title="United States Marine Corps birthday ball">Marine Corps Birthday</a> is celebrated every year on 10 November in a cake-cutting ceremony where the first slice of cake is given to the oldest Marine present, who in turn hands it off to the youngest Marine present. The celebration includes a reading of Commandant <a href="/wiki/John_A._Lejeune" title="John A. Lejeune">Lejeune's</a> Birthday Message.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> Close Order Drill is heavily emphasized early on in a Marine's initial training, incorporated into most formal events, and is used to teach discipline by instilling habits of precision and automatic response to orders, increase the confidence of junior officers and noncommissioned officers through the exercise of command and give Marines an opportunity to handle individual weapons.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>An important part of the Marine Corps culture is the traditional seafaring <a href="/wiki/Glossary_of_nautical_terms" title="Glossary of nautical terms">naval terminology</a> derived from its history with the Navy. <a href="/wiki/Marines" title="Marines">Marines</a> are not "soldiers", or "sailors".<sup id="cite_ref-DCNT92505_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCNT92505-125">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Unofficial_traditions_and_customs">Unofficial traditions and customs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Unofficial traditions and customs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Teufel_Hunden_US_Marines_recruiting_poster.jpg" class="image"><img alt="cartoon of a bulldog wearing a Marine helmet chasing a dachshund wearing a German helmet, the poster reads &quot;Teufelhunden: German nickname for U.S. Marines. Devil Dog recruiting station, 628 South State Street&quot;" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Teufel_Hunden_US_Marines_recruiting_poster.jpg/170px-Teufel_Hunden_US_Marines_recruiting_poster.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="250" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Teufel_Hunden_US_Marines_recruiting_poster.jpg/255px-Teufel_Hunden_US_Marines_recruiting_poster.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Teufel_Hunden_US_Marines_recruiting_poster.jpg/340px-Teufel_Hunden_US_Marines_recruiting_poster.jpg 2x" data-file-width="833" data-file-height="1223" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Teufel_Hunden_US_Marines_recruiting_poster.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A recruiting poster makes use of the "Teufel Hunden" nickname</div></div></div>
<p>Marines have several generic nicknames:
</p>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Devil_Dog" title="Devil Dog">Devil Dog</a></i> German soldiers during the First World War said that at Belleau Wood the Marines were so vicious that the German infantrymen called them Teufel-Hunden – 'devil dogs'.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Gyrene</i> commonly used between fellow Marines.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Leatherneck" title="Leatherneck">Leatherneck</a></i> refers to a leather collar formerly part of the Marine uniform during the Revolutionary War period.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Jarhead</i> has several oft-disputed explanations.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Some other unofficial traditions include mottos and exclamations:
</p>
<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Oorah_(Marines)" class="mw-redirect" title="Oorah (Marines)">Oorah</a></i> is common among Marines, being similar in function and purpose to the Army and Air Force's <a href="/wiki/Hooah" title="Hooah">hooah</a> and the Navy's <a href="/wiki/Hooyah" title="Hooyah">hooyah</a> cries. Many possible <a href="/wiki/Etymology" title="Etymology">etymologies</a> have been offered for the term.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><i>Semper Fi</i> is a common greeting among serving and veteran Marines. It is short for the Marine Corps Motto "Semper Fidelis", which in Latin means "Always Faithful".</li>
<li><i>Improvise, Adapt and Overcome</i> has become an adopted mantra in many units.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Veteran_Marines">Veteran Marines</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Veteran Marines">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Corps encourages the idea that "Marine" is an earned title and most Marine Corps personnel take to heart the phrase "Once a Marine, Always a Marine". They reject the term "ex-Marine" in most circumstances. There are no regulations concerning the address of persons who have left active service, so a number of customary terms have come into common use:<sup id="cite_ref-Krulak_69-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krulak-69">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>"Marine" is acceptable and considered complimentary by most Corps personnel.</li>
<li>An honorably discharged Marine is a "Marine". The title "Marine Corps Veteran" is also acceptable. There are no honorably discharged "Former" or "Ex" Marines.</li>
<li>"Retired Marine" is generally reserved for those who have completed 20 or more years of service are called "Lifers" and formally retired or those who have been medically retired.</li>
<li>According to one of the "Commandant's White letters" from Commandant <a href="/wiki/Alfred_M._Gray,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Alfred M. Gray, Jr.">Alfred M. Gray, Jr.</a>, referring to a Marine by their last earned rank is appropriate.<sup id="cite_ref-Freedman_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Freedman-135">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Martial_arts_program">Martial arts program</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Martial arts program">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marine_martial_arts.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Marine_martial_arts.jpg/220px-Marine_martial_arts.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Marine_martial_arts.jpg/330px-Marine_martial_arts.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/Marine_martial_arts.jpg/440px-Marine_martial_arts.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="714" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marine_martial_arts.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marine training in martial arts</div></div></div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Martial_Arts_Program" title="Marine Corps Martial Arts Program">Marine Corps Martial Arts Program</a></div>
<p>In 2001, the Marine Corps initiated an internally designed martial arts program, called Marine Corps Martial Arts Program (MCMAP). Due to an expectation that urban and police-type <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a> missions would become more common in the 21st century, placing Marines in even closer contact with unarmed civilians, MCMAP was implemented to provide Marines with a larger and more versatile set of less-than-lethal options for controlling hostile, but unarmed individuals. It is a stated aim of the program to instill and maintain the "Warrior Ethos" within Marines.<sup id="cite_ref-Yi_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Yi-136">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The Marine Corps Martial Arts program is an eclectic mix of different styles of martial arts melded together. MCMAP consists of punches and kicks from <a href="/wiki/Taekwondo" title="Taekwondo">Taekwondo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Karate" title="Karate">Karate</a>, opponent weight transfer from <a href="/wiki/Jujitsu" class="mw-redirect" title="Jujitsu">Jujitsu</a>, ground grappling involving <a href="/wiki/Joint_lock" title="Joint lock">joint locking</a> techniques and <a href="/wiki/Chokehold" title="Chokehold">chokes</a> from Brazilian jiu-jitsu, and a mix of knife and baton/stick fighting derived from <a href="/wiki/Eskrima" class="mw-redirect" title="Eskrima">Eskrima</a>, and elbow strikes and kick boxing from <a href="/wiki/Muay_Thai" title="Muay Thai">Muay Thai</a>. Marines begin MCMAP training in boot camp, where they will earn the first of five available <a href="/wiki/Marine_Corps_Martial_Arts_Program#Structure_and_belt_system" title="Marine Corps Martial Arts Program">belts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Equipment">Equipment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Equipment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main pages: <a href="/wiki/Category:United_States_Marine_Corps_equipment" title="Category:United States Marine Corps equipment">Category:United States Marine Corps equipment</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_Marine_Corps_individual_equipment" title="List of United States Marine Corps individual equipment">List of United States Marine Corps individual equipment</a></div>
<p>As of 2013, the typical infantry rifleman carries $14,000 worth of gear (excluding <a href="/wiki/Night_vision_device" class="mw-redirect" title="Night vision device">night-vision goggles</a>), compared to $2,500 a decade earlier. The number of pieces of equipment (everything from radios to trucks) in a typical infantry battalion has also increased, from 3,400 pieces of gear in 2001 to 8,500 in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infantry_weapons">Infantry weapons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States_Marine_Corps&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Infantry weapons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_weapons_of_the_United_States_Marine_Corps" title="List of weapons of the United States Marine Corps">List of weapons of the United States Marine Corps</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FORECON_CQB_trng_-001-.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/FORECON_CQB_trng_-001-.jpg/220px-FORECON_CQB_trng_-001-.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/FORECON_CQB_trng_-001-.jpg/330px-FORECON_CQB_trng_-001-.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/FORECON_CQB_trng_-001-.jpg/440px-FORECON_CQB_trng_-001-.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="997" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FORECON_CQB_trng_-001-.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marines firing the <a href="/wiki/MEU(SOC)_pistol" title="MEU(SOC) pistol">MEU(SOC) pistol</a> while <a href="/wiki/Garrison" title="Garrison">garrisoned</a> aboard a ship</div></div></div>
<p>The basic infantry weapon of the Marine Corps is the <a href="/wiki/M4_Carbine" class="mw-redirect" title="M4 Carbine">M4 Carbine</a>, with a majority of non-infantry Marines equipped with the M16A4 service rifle. The <a href="/wiki/M4_carbine" title="M4 carbine">M4 carbine</a><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Colt_9mm_SMG" title="Colt 9mm SMG">Colt 9mm SMG</a><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> have also been issued. The standard <a href="/wiki/Side_arm" title="Side arm">side arm</a> is the <a href="/wiki/M9_pistol" class="mw-redirect" title="M9 pistol">M9A1 pistol</a>. The Colt <a href="/wiki/M1911A1" class="mw-redirect" title="M1911A1">M1911A1</a> is also being put back into service as the <a href="/wiki/MEU(SOC)_pistol" title="MEU(SOC) pistol">M45A1</a> Close Quarter Battle Pistol (CQBP) in small numbers. <a href="/wiki/Suppressive_fire" title="Suppressive fire">Suppressive fire</a> is provided by the <a href="/wiki/M27_Infantry_Automatic_Rifle" title="M27 Infantry Automatic Rifle">M27 IAR</a>, <a href="/wiki/M249_light_machine_gun" title="M249 light machine gun">M249 SAW</a>, and <a href="/wiki/M240_machine_gun" title="M240 machine gun">M240</a> machine guns, at the squad and company levels respectively. In addition, indirect fire is provided by the <a href="/wiki/M203_grenade_launcher" title="M203 grenade launcher">M203 grenade launcher</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Milkor_MGL" title="Milkor MGL">M32 grenade launcher</a> in fireteams, <a href="/wiki/M224_mortar" title="M224 mortar">M224 60&#160;mm mortar</a> in companies, and <a href="/wiki/M252_mortar" title="M252 mortar">M252 81&#160;mm mortar</a> in battalions. The <a href="/wiki/M2_Browning_machine_gun" class="mw-redirect" title="M2 Browning machine gun">M2 .50&#160;caliber heavy machine gun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mk_19_grenade_launcher" title="Mk 19 grenade launcher">MK19 automatic grenade launcher (40&#160;mm)</a> are available for use by dismounted infantry, though they are more commonly vehicle-mounted. <br />Precision firepower is provided by the <a href="/wiki/M40_rifle" title="M40 rifle">M40 series</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Barrett_M107" class="mw-redirect" title="Barrett M107">Barrett M107</a>, while <a href="/wiki/Designated_marksman" title="Designated marksman">designated marksmen</a> use the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps_Designated_Marksman_Rifle" title="United States Marine Corps Designated Marksman Rifle">DMR</a> (being replaced by the <a href="/wiki/M39_Enhanced_Marksman_Rifle" title="M39 Enhanced Marksman Rifle">M39 EMR</a>), and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps_Squad_Advanced_Marksman_Rifle" title="United States Marine Corps Squad Advanced Marksman Rifle">SAM-R</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
